	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">John Oliver</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">

<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">English comedian and television host</div>

<p><b>John William Oliver</b> (born 23 April 1977)<sup id="cite_ref-biography.com_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-biography.com-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> is an English-American<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> comedian, writer, producer, political commentator, actor, and television host. Oliver started his career as a stand-up comedian, both in the United Kingdom and United States. He came to wider attention for his work on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Show" title="The Daily Show">The Daily Show with Jon Stewart</a></i> as its senior British correspondent from 2006 to 2013. Oliver won three <a href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Award" title="Primetime Emmy Award">Primetime Emmy Awards</a> for his work as a writer on <i>The Daily Show</i> and was its <a href="/wiki/Guest_host" title="Guest host">guest host</a> for an eight-week period in 2013. In addition to <i>The Daily Show</i>, Oliver co-hosted the satirical comedy <a href="/wiki/Podcast" title="Podcast">podcast</a> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Bugle" title="The Bugle">The Bugle</a></i> (2007–2015) with <a href="/wiki/Andy_Zaltzman" title="Andy Zaltzman">Andy Zaltzman</a>, with whom Oliver had previously co-hosted the radio series <i><a href="/wiki/Political_Animal_(radio_show)" title="Political Animal (radio show)">Political Animal</a></i>, and hosted <i><a href="/wiki/John_Oliver%27s_New_York_Stand-Up_Show" title="John Oliver&#39;s New York Stand-Up Show">John Oliver's New York Stand-Up Show</a></i> on <a href="/wiki/Comedy_Central" title="Comedy Central">Comedy Central</a> from 2010 to 2013. He has also acted on television, most notably in a recurring role as Ian Duncan on the <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a> <a href="/wiki/Situation_comedy" class="mw-redirect" title="Situation comedy">sitcom</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Community_(TV_series)" title="Community (TV series)">Community</a></i>, and in films, notably <a href="/wiki/Voice_acting" title="Voice acting">voice-over work</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Smurfs_(film)" title="The Smurfs (film)">The Smurfs</a></i> (2011) and its <a href="/wiki/The_Smurfs_2" title="The Smurfs 2">sequel</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/The_Lion_King_(2019_film)" title="The Lion King (2019 film)">remake of <i>The Lion King</i></a>.
</p><p>Since 2014, Oliver has been the host of the <a href="/wiki/HBO" title="HBO">HBO</a> series <i><a href="/wiki/Last_Week_Tonight_with_John_Oliver" title="Last Week Tonight with John Oliver">Last Week Tonight with John Oliver</a></i>. He has received widespread critical and popular recognition for his work on the series, whose influence over US culture, legislation, and policymaking has been dubbed the "John Oliver effect".<sup id="cite_ref-time.com_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-time.com-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Dekel_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dekel-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> For his work on <i>Last Week Tonight</i>, Oliver has won eight <a href="/wiki/Emmy_Award" title="Emmy Award">Emmy Awards</a> and two <a href="/wiki/Peabody_Award" title="Peabody Award">Peabody Awards</a> and was included in the 2015 <i><a href="/wiki/Time_100" title="Time 100">Time</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Time_100" title="Time 100">100</a>, being described as a "comedic agent of change...powerful because he isn't afraid to tackle important issues thoughtfully, without fear or apology."<sup id="cite_ref-vanf1_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vanf1-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Many have opined that Oliver's work is <a href="/wiki/Journalism" title="Journalism">journalism</a> or <a href="/wiki/Investigative_journalism" title="Investigative journalism">investigative journalism</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> a claim Oliver himself disputes.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life_and_education">Early life and education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_Oliver&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life and education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Oliver was born on 23 April 1977 in <a href="/wiki/Erdington" title="Erdington">Erdington, Birmingham, West Midlands</a>, England,<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> to Carole and Jim Oliver. His father was both a school headmaster and social worker, and his mother was a music teacher. Both of his parents are originally from <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool, Merseyside</a>. His uncle was the composer <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Oliver_(composer)" title="Stephen Oliver (composer)">Stephen Oliver</a>, and <a href="/wiki/William_Boyd_Carpenter" title="William Boyd Carpenter">William Boyd Carpenter</a> was a paternal great-great-grandfather, <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Ripon_(modern_diocese)" title="Bishop of Ripon (modern diocese)">Bishop of Ripon</a> and court chaplain to <a href="/wiki/Queen_Victoria" title="Queen Victoria">Queen Victoria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-vanf1_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vanf1-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since childhood, he has been a fan of <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool FC</a>, noting in interviews that "my mum's family are from <a href="/wiki/Knotty_Ash" title="Knotty Ash">Knotty Ash</a> and my dad's family are from <a href="/wiki/Wirral_Peninsula" title="Wirral Peninsula">the Wirral</a>, so supporting Liverpool was very much not a choice".<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> As a child, Oliver was educated in <a href="/wiki/Bedford" title="Bedford">Bedford</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Mark_Rutherford_School" title="Mark Rutherford School">Mark Rutherford School</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-vanf1_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vanf1-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-guardianinterview_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardianinterview-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Following secondary school, he studied at <a href="/wiki/Christ%27s_College,_Cambridge" title="Christ&#39;s College, Cambridge">Christ's College, Cambridge</a>. While a student there in the mid-to-late 1990s, Oliver was a member of the <a href="/wiki/Footlights" title="Footlights">Cambridge Footlights</a>, the university theatrical club run by students of <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cambridge" title="University of Cambridge">Cambridge University</a>. Oliver's contemporaries in the troupe included <a href="/wiki/David_Mitchell_(comedian)" title="David Mitchell (comedian)">David Mitchell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Richard_Ayoade" title="Richard Ayoade">Richard Ayoade</a>. In 1997, he became the club's vice president.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> In 1998, Oliver graduated from Christ's College with a degree in English.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_Oliver&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stand-up">Stand-up</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_Oliver&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Stand-up">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wyatt_Cenac,_John_Oliver_and_Rory_Albanese_at_Moravian_College.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Wyatt_Cenac%2C_John_Oliver_and_Rory_Albanese_at_Moravian_College.jpg/220px-Wyatt_Cenac%2C_John_Oliver_and_Rory_Albanese_at_Moravian_College.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Wyatt_Cenac%2C_John_Oliver_and_Rory_Albanese_at_Moravian_College.jpg/330px-Wyatt_Cenac%2C_John_Oliver_and_Rory_Albanese_at_Moravian_College.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Wyatt_Cenac%2C_John_Oliver_and_Rory_Albanese_at_Moravian_College.jpg/440px-Wyatt_Cenac%2C_John_Oliver_and_Rory_Albanese_at_Moravian_College.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wyatt_Cenac,_John_Oliver_and_Rory_Albanese_at_Moravian_College.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Wyatt_Cenac" title="Wyatt Cenac">Wyatt Cenac</a>, John Oliver, and <a href="/wiki/Rory_Albanese" title="Rory Albanese">Rory Albanese</a> after performing comedy at <a href="/wiki/Moravian_College" title="Moravian College">Moravian College</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bethlehem,_Pennsylvania" title="Bethlehem, Pennsylvania">Bethlehem, Pennsylvania</a> in April 2009</div></div></div>
<p>Oliver first appeared at the <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Fringe" class="mw-redirect" title="Edinburgh Fringe">Edinburgh Festival Fringe</a> in <a href="/wiki/2001_Edinburgh_Festival_Fringe" class="mw-redirect" title="2001 Edinburgh Festival Fringe">2001</a> as part of <i>The Comedy Zone</i>, a late-night showcase of newer acts, where he played the character of an "oleaginous journalist".<sup id="cite_ref-splitsider_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-splitsider-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> At the Festival and similar venues, Oliver frequently worked with other members of the Chocolate Milk Gang, a group of comedians who often collaborated and performed with one another, including <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Kitson" title="Daniel Kitson">Daniel Kitson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russell_Howard" title="Russell Howard">Russell Howard</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_O%27Doherty" title="David O&#39;Doherty">David O’Doherty</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Alun_Cochrane" title="Alun Cochrane">Alun Cochrane</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> He performed his debut solo show in <a href="/wiki/2002_Edinburgh_Festival_Fringe" class="mw-redirect" title="2002 Edinburgh Festival Fringe">2002</a> and returned in <a href="/wiki/2003_Edinburgh_Festival_Fringe" class="mw-redirect" title="2003 Edinburgh Festival Fringe">2003</a>. In <a href="/wiki/2004_Edinburgh_Festival_Fringe" class="mw-redirect" title="2004 Edinburgh Festival Fringe">2004</a> and <a href="/wiki/2005_Edinburgh_Festival_Fringe" class="mw-redirect" title="2005 Edinburgh Festival Fringe">2005</a>, he collaborated with <a href="/wiki/Andy_Zaltzman" title="Andy Zaltzman">Andy Zaltzman</a> on a <a href="/wiki/Double_act" title="Double act">double act</a> and co-hosting <i><a href="/wiki/Political_Animal_(radio)" class="mw-redirect" title="Political Animal (radio)">Political Animal</a></i>, with various acts performing political material.
</p><p>After moving to New York City for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Show" title="The Daily Show">The Daily Show</a></i>, Oliver began performing stand-up in small clubs around the city and later headlined shows in larger venues.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Oliver's first stand-up special, titled <i>John Oliver: Terrifying Times</i>, debuted on <a href="/wiki/Comedy_Central" title="Comedy Central">Comedy Central</a> in 2008 and was later released on DVD.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Since 2010, Oliver has hosted four seasons of <i><a href="/wiki/John_Oliver%27s_New_York_Stand-Up_Show" title="John Oliver&#39;s New York Stand-Up Show">John Oliver's New York Stand-Up Show</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> In 2013, he went to Afghanistan on a USO tour to perform stand-up for the troops there.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to Edward Helmore in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i>, "His style leans toward the kind that Americans like best from the British – exaggerated, full of odd accents and mannerisms, in the vein of <a href="/wiki/Monty_Python" title="Monty Python">Monty Python</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-guardianinterview_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardianinterview-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Oliver has used his British culture as a primary subject of his jokes.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Oliver describes his own accent as a "mongrel" of <a href="/wiki/Brummie#Accent" class="mw-redirect" title="Brummie">Brummie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scouse" title="Scouse">Scouse</a>, and <a href="/wiki/English_in_southern_England#Bedfordshire" class="mw-redirect" title="English in southern England">Bedford</a> influences.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Oliver continues to perform stand up.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mock_the_Week"><i>Mock the Week</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_Oliver&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Mock the Week">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Prior to joining <i>The Daily Show</i>, Oliver was making appearances on British television as a panellist on the satirical news quiz <i><a href="/wiki/Mock_the_Week" title="Mock the Week">Mock the Week</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-splitsider_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-splitsider-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> He was a frequent guest on the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Mock_the_Week_episodes" title="List of Mock the Week episodes">first two series</a> in 2005 and 2006, appearing in 7 out of 11 episodes.<sup id="cite_ref-splitsider_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-splitsider-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Daily_Show_with_Jon_Stewart"><i>The Daily Show with Jon Stewart</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_Oliver&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: The Daily Show with Jon Stewart">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:John_Oliver_Wyatt_Cenac_hug_Shankbone.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/John_Oliver_Wyatt_Cenac_hug_Shankbone.jpg/220px-John_Oliver_Wyatt_Cenac_hug_Shankbone.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/John_Oliver_Wyatt_Cenac_hug_Shankbone.jpg/330px-John_Oliver_Wyatt_Cenac_hug_Shankbone.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/John_Oliver_Wyatt_Cenac_hug_Shankbone.jpg/440px-John_Oliver_Wyatt_Cenac_hug_Shankbone.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3340" data-file-height="2504" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:John_Oliver_Wyatt_Cenac_hug_Shankbone.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Oliver and <a href="/wiki/Wyatt_Cenac" title="Wyatt Cenac">Wyatt Cenac</a> at the launch of <i><a href="/wiki/Earth_(The_Book)" title="Earth (The Book)">Earth</a></i></div></div></div>
<p>Oliver joined <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Show_with_Jon_Stewart" class="mw-redirect" title="The Daily Show with Jon Stewart">The Daily Show with Jon Stewart</a></i> as its Senior British Correspondent in July 2006. He says he was interviewed for the show on the recommendation of comedian <a href="/wiki/Ricky_Gervais" title="Ricky Gervais">Ricky Gervais</a>, who had never met Oliver, but was familiar with his work.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> It was his first time in the United States. Two weeks after the interview, he got the job, flying from London to New York on a Sunday and unexpectedly appearing on camera the next day.<sup id="cite_ref-thrhbo_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thrhbo-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Oliver received <a href="/wiki/Emmy_Award" title="Emmy Award">Emmy Awards</a> for outstanding writing in 2009, 2011, and 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the summer of 2013, Oliver <a href="/wiki/Guest_host" title="Guest host">guest-hosted</a> <i>The Daily Show</i> for eight weeks while Stewart directed his movie <i><a href="/wiki/Rosewater_(film)" title="Rosewater (film)">Rosewater</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-guesthost_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guesthost-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Oliver's performance received positive reviews,<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> with some critics suggesting that he should eventually succeed Stewart as host of <i>The Daily Show</i> or receive his own show.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> CBS discussed the possibility of Oliver replacing <a href="/wiki/Craig_Ferguson" title="Craig Ferguson">Craig Ferguson</a> on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Late_Late_Show_with_Craig_Ferguson" title="The Late Late Show with Craig Ferguson">The Late Late Show</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-thrhbo_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thrhbo-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Three months after his <i>Daily Show</i> hosting, HBO announced it was giving Oliver his own late-night show.<sup id="cite_ref-HBO_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HBO-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Bugle"><i>The Bugle</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_Oliver&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: The Bugle">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>From October 2007 to May 2015, Oliver co-hosted <i><a href="/wiki/The_Bugle" title="The Bugle">The Bugle</a></i>, a weekly satirical comedy <a href="/wiki/Podcast" title="Podcast">podcast</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Andy_Zaltzman" title="Andy Zaltzman">Andy Zaltzman</a>. Originally produced by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a></i> of London, it became an independent project in 2012. Its 200th episode aired on 13 July 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> The show reached a download count of 500,000 times a month.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="John_Oliver.27s_New_York_Stand-Up_Show"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="John_Oliver's_New_York_Stand-Up_Show"><i>John Oliver's New York Stand-Up Show</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_Oliver&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: John Oliver&#039;s New York Stand-Up Show">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2009, Comedy Central announced that it would be ordering six episodes of the Oliver hosted <i><a href="/wiki/John_Oliver%27s_New_York_Stand-Up_Show" title="John Oliver&#39;s New York Stand-Up Show">John Oliver's New York Stand-Up Show</a></i>, a stand-up series on Comedy Central that featured sets from himself and other stand-up comedians, including <a href="/wiki/Janeane_Garofalo" title="Janeane Garofalo">Janeane Garofalo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brian_Posehn" title="Brian Posehn">Brian Posehn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_F._Tompkins" title="Paul F. Tompkins">Paul F. Tompkins</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marc_Maron" title="Marc Maron">Marc Maron</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hibberd_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hibberd-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Oliver executively produced the show along with Avalon Television's Richard Allen-Turner, David Martin, James Taylor and <a href="/wiki/Jon_Thoday" title="Jon Thoday">Jon Thoday</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hibberd_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hibberd-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Each episode featured four comics.<sup id="cite_ref-Hibberd_49-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hibberd-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> From 2010 to 2013, four seasons of the show were produced, the final lasting eight episodes.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Last_Week_Tonight"><i>Last Week Tonight</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_Oliver&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Last Week Tonight">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Last_Week_Tonight_with_John_Oliver" title="Last Week Tonight with John Oliver">Last Week Tonight with John Oliver</a></div>
<p>Oliver began hosting <i><a href="/wiki/Last_Week_Tonight_with_John_Oliver" title="Last Week Tonight with John Oliver">Last Week Tonight with John Oliver</a></i>, a <a href="/wiki/Late-night_talk_show" title="Late-night talk show">late-night talk show</a> that takes a satirical look at news, politics, and current events, on 27 April 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> His initial two-year contract with HBO was extended through 2017 in February 2015,<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> and through 2020 in September 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Oliver says he has full creative freedom, including free rein to criticize corporations, given HBO's ad-free subscription model.<sup id="cite_ref-thrhbo_35-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thrhbo-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> His work on the show led to Oliver being named on the list of <a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)"><i>Time</i> magazine's</a> <a href="/wiki/Time_100" title="Time 100">"100 Most Influential People"</a> in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2018, <i>Last Week Tonight</i> was honoured with a <a href="/wiki/Peabody_Award" title="Peabody Award">Peabody Award</a> in the "Entertainment" category for "bringing satire and journalism even closer together,"<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> at the 77th Annual Peabody Awards.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Television_acting">Television acting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_Oliver&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Television acting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As a boy, Oliver played Felix Pardiggle, a minor role in the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> drama <i><a href="/wiki/Bleak_House_(1985_TV_serial)" title="Bleak House (1985 TV serial)">Bleak House</a></i> in 1985.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Oliver had a recurring role on the <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a> comedy <i><a href="/wiki/Community_(TV_series)" title="Community (TV series)">Community</a></i> as psychology professor Ian Duncan.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> However, he declined becoming a regular cast member of the series because he did not want to leave <i>The Daily Show</i> for it. He did not appear in the show's third and fourth seasons, but returned in season five, appearing in seven of its 13 episodes. He was not in season six which aired on <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!" title="Yahoo!">Yahoo!</a><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Oliver has also worked on <i><a href="/wiki/Gravity_Falls" title="Gravity Falls">Gravity Falls</a></i> as the voice of Sherlock Holmes (season 1, episode 3), <i><a href="/wiki/Rick_and_Morty" title="Rick and Morty">Rick and Morty</a></i> as an amoeba named Dr. Xenon Bloom (season 1, episode 3), <i><a href="/wiki/People_Like_Us_(mockumentary)" title="People Like Us (mockumentary)">People Like Us</a></i> as a bank manager (season 2, episode 5), <i><a href="/wiki/Randy_Cunningham:_9th_Grade_Ninja" title="Randy Cunningham: 9th Grade Ninja">Randy Cunningham: 9th Grade Ninja</a></i> as the voice of Coach Green (season 1, episode 9), <i><a href="/wiki/My_Hero_(UK_TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="My Hero (UK TV series)">My Hero</a></i> as a man from the BBC (season 2, episode 5), <i><a href="/wiki/Green_Wing" title="Green Wing">Green Wing</a></i> as a car salesman (season 1, episode 1), and <i><a href="/wiki/Bob%27s_Burgers" title="Bob&#39;s Burgers">Bob's Burgers</a></i> as a cat agent (season 7, episode 10).
</p><p>Oliver guest starred as Booth Wilkes-John<sup id="cite_ref-bwj_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bwj-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> in the <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_(season_25)" title="The Simpsons (season 25)">25th season</a> episode "<a href="/wiki/Pay_Pal_(The_Simpsons)" title="Pay Pal (The Simpsons)">Pay Pal</a>", of the <a href="/wiki/Fox_Broadcasting_Company" title="Fox Broadcasting Company">FOX</a> animated television series <i><a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons" title="The Simpsons">The Simpsons</a></i>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Film">Film</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_Oliver&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Film">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2008, Oliver was given his first film role, playing Dick Pants in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Love_Guru" title="The Love Guru">The Love Guru</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> He later voiced Vanity Smurf in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Smurfs_(film)" title="The Smurfs (film)">The Smurfs</a></i> film and its <a href="/wiki/The_Smurfs_2" title="The Smurfs 2">sequel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> He was originally cast in 2010 to star in the <a href="/wiki/Terry_Jones" title="Terry Jones">Terry Jones</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/Absolutely_Anything" title="Absolutely Anything">Absolutely Anything</a></i> as Neil Clarke,<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> but scheduling conflicts due to the debut of <i><a href="/wiki/Last_Week_Tonight_with_John_Oliver" title="Last Week Tonight with John Oliver">Last Week Tonight</a></i> in 2014 led to the role being recast for <a href="/wiki/Simon_Pegg" title="Simon Pegg">Simon Pegg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> In 2019, Oliver voiced porcupine Steve in the CGI animation <i><a href="/wiki/Wonder_Park" title="Wonder Park">Wonder Park</a></i> and hornbill <a href="/wiki/List_of_The_Lion_King_characters#Zazu" title="List of The Lion King characters">Zazu</a> in the <a href="/wiki/The_Lion_King_(2019_film)" title="The Lion King (2019 film)">remake</a> of Disney's <i>The Lion King</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_work">Other work</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_Oliver&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Other work">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Oliver wrote and presented a <a href="/wiki/BBC_America" title="BBC America">BBC America</a> campaign to have viewers use <a href="/wiki/Closed_captioning" title="Closed captioning">closed captioning</a> (<a href="/wiki/Subtitles" title="Subtitles">subtitles</a>). Shown in brief segments before shows, "The following program contains accents you would have heard a lot more if you hadn't <a href="/wiki/Boston_Tea_Party" title="Boston Tea Party">thrown our tea into Boston Harbour</a>," says one. "Not even British people can follow the British accent 100 percent of the time. Therefore you, like me, might want to use closed-captioning." Oliver used some of these jokes in his stand-up routine.<sup id="cite_ref-Lafayette_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lafayette-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Oliver frequently appeared on the <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_5_Live" title="BBC Radio 5 Live">BBC Radio 5 Live</a> sports show <i><a href="/wiki/Fighting_Talk" title="Fighting Talk">Fighting Talk</a></i>.
</p><p>From 2002 to 2003, Oliver worked on the <a href="/wiki/BBC_Three" title="BBC Three">BBC 3</a> comedy series <i>The State We're In</i>, along with <a href="/wiki/Anita_Rani" title="Anita Rani">Anita Rani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jon_Holmes" title="Jon Holmes">Jon Holmes</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Robin_Ince" title="Robin Ince">Robin Ince</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2003, Oliver manned the "results desk" on an election night episode of <a href="/wiki/Armando_Iannucci" title="Armando Iannucci">Armando Iannucci</a>'s satirical show <i><a href="/wiki/Gash_(TV_series)" title="Gash (TV series)">Gash</a></i> on <a href="/wiki/Channel_4" title="Channel 4">Channel 4</a>. He would work with Iannucci again in 2005, as a panellist in the second episode of <i><a href="/wiki/Armando_Iannucci%27s_Charm_Offensive" title="Armando Iannucci&#39;s Charm Offensive">Armando Iannucci's Charm Offensive</a></i>.
</p><p>In 2004, Oliver wrote and performed in the satirical radio program <i><a href="/wiki/The_Department" title="The Department">The Department</a></i> on <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_4" title="BBC Radio 4">BBC Radio 4</a>, with frequent comedy partner <a href="/wiki/Andy_Zaltzman" title="Andy Zaltzman">Andy Zaltzman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chris_Addison" title="Chris Addison">Chris Addison</a>. He portrayed the character Victor Gooch for all three series, prior to the cancellation of the program in 2006.
</p><p>Oliver performed various roles in the 2009 <a href="/wiki/Comedy_Central" title="Comedy Central">Comedy Central</a> series <i><a href="/wiki/Important_Things_with_Demetri_Martin" title="Important Things with Demetri Martin">Important Things with Demetri Martin</a></i>.
</p><p>In 2009, Oliver made a cameo appearance as the actor <a href="/wiki/Rip_Torn" title="Rip Torn">Rip Torn</a> in the music video for <a href="/wiki/The_Fiery_Furnaces" title="The Fiery Furnaces">the Fiery Furnaces</a> single "Even in the Rain", which is based on the story of the making of the film <i><a href="/wiki/Easy_Rider" title="Easy Rider">Easy Rider</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2018, Oliver began working as an executive producer for <i><a href="/wiki/Wyatt_Cenac%E2%80%99s_Problem_Areas" class="mw-redirect" title="Wyatt Cenac’s Problem Areas">Wyatt Cenac’s Problem Areas</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Influence_and_the_.22John_Oliver_effect.22"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Influence_and_the_&quot;John_Oliver_effect&quot;">Influence and the "John Oliver effect"</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_Oliver&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Influence and the &quot;John Oliver effect&quot;">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:John_Oliver_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/John_Oliver_1.jpg/170px-John_Oliver_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/John_Oliver_1.jpg/255px-John_Oliver_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/John_Oliver_1.jpg/340px-John_Oliver_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="4508" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:John_Oliver_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Oliver speaking at the 2014 <a href="/wiki/Crunchies" title="Crunchies">Crunchies</a></div></div></div>
<p>Oliver has said that among his comedic influences are: <a href="/wiki/Armando_Iannucci" title="Armando Iannucci">Armando Iannucci</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Letterman" title="David Letterman">David Letterman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monty_Python" title="Monty Python">Monty Python</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Cook" title="Peter Cook">Peter Cook</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Pryor" title="Richard Pryor">Richard Pryor</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Jon_Stewart" title="Jon Stewart">Jon Stewart</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> On Monty Python he states, "citing them as an influence is almost redundant. It’s assumed. I saw <i><a href="/wiki/Monty_Python%27s_Life_of_Brian" title="Monty Python&#39;s Life of Brian">Life of Brian</a></i> in middle school, when a substitute teacher put it on to keep us quiet on a rainy day. I’m not sure he knew exactly what he was showing us, but I’ve always been hugely grateful for the reckless professional mistake he made that day, because I’ve never forgotten how it made me feel."<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Oliver's comedic commentary has been credited with helping influence US legislation, regulations, court rulings, and other aspects of US culture; this influence has been dubbed "The John Oliver effect".<sup id="cite_ref-time.com_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-time.com-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Dekel_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dekel-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> This came from <a href="/wiki/Net_Neutrality_(Last_Week_Tonight)#&quot;Net_Neutrality&quot;" title="Net Neutrality (Last Week Tonight)">the show's fifth episode</a>, which dealt with <a href="/wiki/Net_neutrality" title="Net neutrality">net neutrality</a>, a subject that had previously been considered obscure and technical.<sup id="cite_ref-transform_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-transform-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Oliver documented problems attributed to internet service providers and argued that the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Communications_Commission" title="Federal Communications Commission">Federal Communications Commission</a> (FCC) could resolve these concerns with upcoming changes to internet regulation. Oliver then encouraged viewers to submit public comments through the FCC's website. The FCC's website promptly crashed.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Internal FCC emails revealed the clip was being watched inside the agency.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> FCC Chairman <a href="/wiki/Tom_Wheeler" title="Tom Wheeler">Tom Wheeler</a> publicly addressed the video.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> The FCC was flooded with 3.7 million comments on the subject, by far the most for any issue in the agency's history.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Reporters detected a shift in the FCC's stance: Before Oliver's segment, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> described an FCC proposal that would leave net neutrality "all but dead,"<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> but the paper later said that chairman Wheeler showed "a steady shift toward stronger regulation."<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> Ultimately, the FCC enacted robust net neutrality rules that classified broadband internet service as a public utility.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Oliver was credited with transforming the net neutrality debate.<sup id="cite_ref-transform_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-transform-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A <a href="/wiki/United_States_Court_of_Appeals_for_the_Ninth_Circuit" title="United States Court of Appeals for the Ninth Circuit">Ninth Circuit Court</a> judge cited a <i>Last Week Tonight</i> segment about the lesser constitutional rights of residents of <a href="/wiki/United_States_territory" class="mw-redirect" title="United States territory">US territories</a> in a ruling in favour of the residents of <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">Guam</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;a&#93;</a></sup> Members of <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">Congress</a> credited Oliver with helping win a vote to enforce protections for chicken farmers who speak out about industry practices after a <i>Last Week Tonight</i> segment aired on the subject.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;b&#93;</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a> council member proposed a resolution in Oliver's honour after he aired a segment on the district's <a href="/wiki/District_of_Columbia_statehood_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="District of Columbia statehood movement">struggle to attain statehood</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;c&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Oliver maintains that he is not a journalist,<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> but reporters have argued that his show does engage in journalism.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Peabody_Award" title="Peabody Award">Peabody Awards</a> honoured Oliver, saying his program engages in "investigative reports that 'real' news programs would do well to emulate".<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> One example of Oliver's investigative work is a segment on The <a href="/wiki/Miss_America" title="Miss America">Miss America</a> Organization, which bills itself as "the world's largest provider of scholarships for women."<sup id="cite_ref-citypages_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-citypages-97">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> Oliver's team, which includes four researchers with journalism backgrounds,<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> collected and analysed the organization's state and federal tax forms to find that the organization's scholarship program only distributes a small fraction of its claimed "$45 million made available annually".<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Oliver said that at the national level, the Miss America Organization and Miss America Foundation together spent only $482,000 in cash scholarships in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-citypages_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-citypages-97">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> Oliver found that at the state level, The <a href="/wiki/Miss_Alabama" title="Miss Alabama">Miss Alabama</a> Pageant claimed that it had provided $2,592,000 in scholarships to <a href="/wiki/Troy_University" title="Troy University">Troy University</a> despite not actually distributing any such scholarships.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> The official YouTube video of Oliver's Miss America segment has been viewed more than 15 million times.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Women_Engineers" title="Society of Women Engineers">Society of Women Engineers</a> said Oliver's mention of their scholarship in his story led to $25,000 in donations in the first two days after the episode.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Oliver has also founded and legally incorporated a church, <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Perpetual_Exemption" title="Our Lady of Perpetual Exemption">Our Lady of Perpetual Exemption</a>, to demonstrate how easy it is to qualify as a church and receive tax exempt status in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> The church was created in conjunction with a segment on televangelists who have tax-free mansions and private jets funded by millions of dollars in donations, which are sent in the belief that money given to televangelists can result in God rewarding donors with money, blessings, and cured diseases.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;d&#93;</a></sup> The next week, Oliver showed off the large quantity of unsolicited donations mailed to him.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> The church's website stated that donations would go to <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A9decins_Sans_Fronti%C3%A8res" title="Médecins Sans Frontières">Doctors Without Borders</a> upon the church's dissolution.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Oliver's <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump_(Last_Week_Tonight)" title="Donald Trump (Last Week Tonight)">February 2016 segment</a> on presidential candidate <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a> received over 85 million views on Facebook and YouTube within a month, and was reportedly the "most watched piece of HBO content ever".<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> A network spokesperson said on the piece, "this is a record for any piece of HBO content".<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> In 2018 on Last Week Tonight, Oliver presented <a href="/wiki/A_Day_in_the_Life_of_Marlon_Bundo" title="A Day in the Life of Marlon Bundo">A Day in the Life of Marlon Bundo</a>, a gay parody of <a href="/wiki/Marlon_Bundo%27s_A_Day_in_the_Life_of_the_Vice_President" title="Marlon Bundo&#39;s A Day in the Life of the Vice President">Marlon Bundo's A Day in the Life of the Vice President</a> with <a href="/wiki/Marlon_Bundo#Children&#39;s_books" title="Marlon Bundo">Marlon Bundo</a> as protagonist.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_Oliver&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:John_Oliver_and_Kate_Norley_(31202364806)_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/John_Oliver_and_Kate_Norley_%2831202364806%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-John_Oliver_and_Kate_Norley_%2831202364806%29_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="205" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/John_Oliver_and_Kate_Norley_%2831202364806%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-John_Oliver_and_Kate_Norley_%2831202364806%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/John_Oliver_and_Kate_Norley_%2831202364806%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-John_Oliver_and_Kate_Norley_%2831202364806%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1349" data-file-height="1259" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:John_Oliver_and_Kate_Norley_(31202364806)_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Oliver and Norley in 2016</div></div></div>
<p>Oliver lives in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> with his wife Kate Norley, an <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War" title="Iraq War">Iraq War</a> veteran who served as a <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army" title="United States Army">United States Army</a> <a href="/wiki/Medic" title="Medic">medic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> Oliver has said that they met at the <a href="/wiki/2008_Republican_National_Convention" title="2008 Republican National Convention">2008 Republican National Convention</a>; he was doing a piece for <i>The Daily Show</i> and Norley was campaigning with <a href="/wiki/Vets_for_Freedom" class="mw-redirect" title="Vets for Freedom">Vets for Freedom</a>. She and other veterans hid Oliver, the other correspondents, and the camera crew from security.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> The two married in October 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-biography.com_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-biography.com-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Together, the couple have two sons, one born prematurely<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> in 2015<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> and one born in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-People2018_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-People2018-119">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> Oliver occasionally wears a <a href="/wiki/1st_Cavalry_Division_(United_States)" title="1st Cavalry Division (United States)">1st Cavalry Division</a> lapel pin – his wife's unit in Iraq.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> He has a younger sister who lives in Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Oliver's immigration status placed certain constraints on what he could do in his adopted country, but also provided him with comedy material as he poked fun at the opacity and occasional absurdity of the process of obtaining <a href="/wiki/Permanent_residence_(United_States)" class="mw-redirect" title="Permanent residence (United States)">US residency</a>. Oliver was one of the many writers on the <a href="/wiki/Picketing_(protest)" class="mw-redirect" title="Picketing (protest)">picket lines</a> during the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%932008_Writers_Guild_of_America_strike" class="mw-redirect" title="2007–2008 Writers Guild of America strike">Writers' Guild strike</a>, which brought <i>The Daily Show</i> to a halt;<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> he appeared on the show upon its resuming production on 7 January 2008. During a sketch, he pointed out that he was then in America on a <a href="/wiki/Visa_(document)" class="mw-redirect" title="Visa (document)">visitors' visa</a> that requires him not to strike while the show is in production, as violation of the terms of the visa would be grounds for deportation.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> When asked about his residency status in early 2009, Oliver said, "It's an ongoing, and slightly unsettling, battle to be honest. I tried engraving 'Give me your tired, your poor, and your aspiring comic performers' into the base of the <a href="/wiki/Statue_of_Liberty" title="Statue of Liberty">Statue of Liberty</a>, but apparently that's not legally binding."<sup id="cite_ref-Comic_Crumpet_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Comic_Crumpet-124">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In an episode of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Bugle" title="The Bugle">The Bugle</a></i> released 2 November 2009, and recorded on 30 October 2009, Oliver announced he "finally got approved for [his] <a href="/wiki/United_States_Permanent_Resident_Card" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Permanent Resident Card">green card</a>" (for US residency), noting that now he can "get arrested filming bits for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Show" title="The Daily Show">The Daily Show</a></i>".<sup id="cite_ref-Bugle_94_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bugle_94-125">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> Oliver says he was given a scare when applying at the <a href="/wiki/Embassy_of_the_United_States,_London" title="Embassy of the United States, London">United States embassy in London</a>, when an immigration officer asked, "Give me one good reason I should let you back in to insult my country," which the officer followed up with, "Oh, I'm just kidding, I love the show." Since then, he has referred to Americans as "us" or "you" based on what each segment has demanded.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> Oliver became a US citizen on 13 December 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Oliver's philanthropy includes an on-air giveaway in which he forgave over $15&#160;million of medical debt owed by over 9,000 people. He purchased the debt for $60,000 and forgave it on his show of 4 June in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
